< Review>
Updated review 5/1/2021.  Today I had their two meat omelette. It contains avocado, bacon, bell peppers, cheese, sausage, onion and spinach. The omelette didn't have much depth and was flat. For $10.50, the omelette comes with a juice or latte. I opted for coffee for $2 extra. Their coffee was decent. It is much better than the Folgers coffee most Chinese restaurants serve. I wasn't quite full after the tasty little thin omelette. A Macau pork chop bun was ordered for takeout in case I get hungry later.

Original review:
Indoor brunch today 3/20/21. The interior of the restaurant felt like a contemporary beer brew house/wine tasting room with brick and wood decor. Jojo's Cafe have three indoor tables and four outdoor tables at their parklet for COVID. They offer American style breakfast specials, Vietnamese entrees such as garlic noodles and pho and Hong Kong style cafe dishes such baked pork chops spaghetti and instant noodles (they call it "ramen" on their menu.) I had the corned beef hash, eggs over easy, hash browns, sausage breakfast plate $9 and pork chops instant noodles $6. In tradition with Hong Kong style cafes, the food came out within five minutes. The waitress was really busy with to-go overs and other customers with all seven tables full at 11am. The golden crispy hash browns and over easy style eggs were acceptable. The corned beef hash and sausage were salty and missed their mark on texture. The broth on my pork chops instant noodles was  overpowered with a vegetable soup taste. The chef put too much broccoli and lettuce in there. I would have preferred the seasoning pack that came with Top Ramen. A traditional tomato based Hong Kong style cafe broth would have worked too. The egg and pork chop were good though. My bill was $20 with tax and tip.<//Review>

<rating>5<//rating>< Review>
Cute, cozy, modern cafe serving breakfast, lunch, and dinner. A good portion of the food is build your own entree: rice bowl, soup bowl, or noodle plate. The rest of the food is brunch or the usual Cantonese cafe food. The food is clean, not too salty, and portions are not oversized. They accept credit card with no minimum and deliver. This cafe serves traditional Cantonese cafe food without the usual cash only payment option.<//Review>

< Review>
This new and improved JoJo's is now very obviously geared towards a younger generation with the cute decor and "pay before you eat" system. They also serve a lot of Vietnamese food now which is kinda strange because I always thought of this place as Hong Kong-ese. In any case, I feel like the crowd here is the same: older folks and persons who want a quick meal alone.

I come here quite often actually and it's mainly because of their 3.99 BREAKFAST! No where else can you get an egg, bacon/sausage, slice of toast, and hash browns/french toast/pancake for 3.99.

Another plus, the Hong Kong milk tea is as close as you can get to an actual authentic milk tea in America (according to my parents who are from Hong Kong).</Review>

<UserId.>109276322305123337870</UserId.><username>Brian Hou</username>< time>
1566792279993< /time>
<Rate>5< /Rate><text>Jo Jo's is one of my go-to places for clean Chinese food. It turns out they recently switched to serving Vietnamese food but kept a few of their previous items. I was a little skeptical but decided to give it a shot. I'm glad I did! I was torn between their Beef Noodle Soup and the Laksa. I'm a huge fan of Laksa and opted for the Vietnamese noodles instead. Also ordered a Macaroni Soup with sausages and an egg for the kids which they inhaled. The Laksa is one of the better ones I've had. Broth was well balanced in taste and texture. It was not too thick and not too light, just right. It wasn't over powered with the coconut flavor so you can taste the subtle hint of shrimp paste. I believe it's usually served with the vermicelli but I went with the Vietnamese noodles instead since it can carry more of the flavor of the soup. Customer service was impeccable. I'm one of those customers that need to customize everything and have to have it just the way I want and they gave me just that. Suggestions were taken and requests were fulfilled. Full and satisfied belly at the end of the night. I really couldn't have asked for more. I"ll definitely be back for the Beef Noodle Soup!< /text>< pictures>

< Review>
Sadly JoJo's Chinese menu is gone. Those fantastic salt and pepper chicken wings are no more. Its the same owners but they've changed the restaurant to a Vietnamese restaurant. They also rearranged some of the furniture. Decided to give them a try and I just found it to be bland Vietnamese food. Nothing really special about it. They still have chicken wings on the menu but now it's 4 pieces for $6. I asked if they were under new management but all they said is that the cook had changed. I hope they do well and stay in business but without their old menu and Pho Ha Tien being right down the block doesn't leave me much reason to go back.< /Review>

< text>
Couple of pet peeves of mine: when I ask for extra pickles, I expect the cook to know NOT to just put them all in a single clump, and, when I go to a restaurant like BK in the U.S. I expect to be able to order in english. The food itself was good, hot and as expected  (other than the clump of pickles). I thought it odd that at 12noon there was literally 1 other customer inside and 1 in drive thru -- odd until I tried to order, when I realized no one in the place appeared to speak english. Lucky for me, and surprisingly to the cashier, I am fluent in spanish. The restaurant was clean and well maintained inside, but there were a number of transients sleeping, looking in trash bins, etc all around the property -- not a location I'd visit after dusk.</text>

I visited AFC Urgent Care Bonita because I was experiencing mild-moderate chest pain and breathing discomfort. The check-in process was very easy. <user>102330294009146773607<//user><username>Anatoly Petkov< /username><time>1517774575015< /time>< Rating>
3</Rating>
<Text>Here is the latest victim of the Sour Coffee Trend! Yes, they will hide behind terms like "Lighter Brew" or "Fruit Forward Acidity" but the bottom line is that the coffee is sour. Don't get me wrong, I'm always among the first to experiment and attempt tweaks with anything that's food or drink, but as much as I like trying new things, one thing in espresso culture seems to remain constant - the classic Italian espresso roast. As this could be a very long discussion, we'll leave it to the specialized forums. I'll just say that I prefer to enjoy a tasty balanced coffee instead of tearing from acidity just so I can be fashionable.
Tried a few different things here: 1) Breve Macchiato - very acidic. 2) Cortado - the acidity is diluted with much more milk, which makes it downright watery and bland 3) 2 different types of cold brew - Ethiopian (more fruitiness in the acidity, so more tolerable) and Tanzanian, which was very straightforward.
Refill uses coffee from Bird Rock roasters and they have a variety of blends, so maybe simply offer a lower acidity option as an option for patrons. Just putting that out there...
On to the food. Proof that two good things don't make a great one was my savory crepe breakfast. The menu described it as a crepe with egg, ham and Gruyere cheese. Somehow I missed the fact that there is also hummus in it. I love me some good hummus and as hummus goes, this one is pretty good but believe you me, the combo between the Swiss classic and the Middle Eastern standard is, well...underwhelming.
The paradox was continued in the crepe that my buddy Krash ordered, which had so much salty, smoky bacon that nothing else could be tasted in this otherwise beautiful plate of food. OK, I understand the temptation to give your customers more for their money, but here in the Land of Plenty sometimes less is more. This is one of those cases.
In conclusion, may I suggest that the hummus be offered as a side, and let the final user decide where to put it? Further, please reduce by half the amount of Gruyere in this recipe; add some Bechamel if you think there should be sauce in it - it will probably be a better compliment to the cheese and ham than the hummus. Ditto for the bacon.
All in all Refill is a lovely place and with very little adjustments it could be Great! Will check back in a month or so.
A year later: Either coffee has improved or I'm getting used to the lighter roasts with higher acidity. I like the coffee a bit more than initially, so I'm changing my rating from 3 to 4 out of 5. Avo toast with truffle oil doesn't hurt either. I wish they would have it on whole grain toast but let's be realistic - people love white bread.<//Text><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMbk5EpF47HFXVQde6dQkwkwyNyAlkr8F9MR55H=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pictures><response>None<//response>< gmap_id>

<UserId.>103716035855494263036< /UserId.><username>Gary Oakes< /username><Time>1359420820102</Time>< Rate>
4< /Rate>
< Text>
Of the many Vietnamese restaurants in PB and La Jolla, this hidden gem tops my short list.  Located in a quiet corner of Pacific Plaza next to the Enterprise Car Rental, this family owned restaurant serves up high quality authentic cuisine which is consistent and affordable.  The Pho is excellent and the fresh spring rolls are second only to Brodard in Westminster. My favorite is the grilled pork. Don't confuse this place with the Green Papaya which occupied this space previously.  Pho Time introduced good food, comfortable seating and lots of friendliness to this quiet oasis in the middle of busy PB.  The restaurant is airy with high ceilings, lots of booths and exotic fish tanks.  Check out the rare fish with the giant lump.  You won't be disappointed.</Text>

<Rate>4< /Rate><Review>one of the classier pho places in SD.

overall, I thought my pho had wonderful flavor. i was swayed by a posted photo of the seafood pho -- but I wouldnt recommend getting as a majority (all?) of the seafood was "seafood." it had things that looked like lobster, looked like scallops, etc...but please, for the price tag I should have known better :) I guess most of this stuff is seafood paste of some variety and has a congealed tofu-like texture. maybe it is tofu, i dont know.

but even though everything was mock seafood (except the shrimp...pretty sure that was shrimp but ive been amazed by vegan "shrimp" so who knows) it still has a higher price tag than standard items like the rare beef or chicken - $8.50 I believe. I'm not saying it didnt taste good, I just dont think its worth it. I'll come back and get the aforementioned instead. Someone in my party got the chicken and really enjoyed - said it was basically an entire white meat chicken in there.

my cousin raved about "complimentary" side bread for dipping. i believe its the bread used for the Banh m√¨'s. ya well...its not complimentary, they charge $1.50 for it. definitely good but not worth the price. ill admit my dining for pho is mainly for cheap, quick, and delicious. so when i pay unnecessary extras like "seafood" and "bread" to make it over $10, i realize i did it wrong. also, if my tummy is gonna hurt from the weirdness of components and MSG one way or another, it might as well be cheap!

all in all, pho time is worthy of its popularity...just make sure you order right. i was also given the heads up from a friend to order the rare beef on the side and put in on your own to ensure it doesnt get overcooked. good idea!< /Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Response>

<user_name>Lisa M Styve</user_name>< Review>
Food was not as ordered, again. This facility has continued to demonstrate inconsistency in actually providing what is ordered for pick up or delivery. We've been assured each time, it won't happen again; it always does.

To stay happy when buying from this restaurant, follow these guidelines: Order menu items exactly as offered, do not use option of "on the side", or "hold mayonnaise or red sauce", and you may possibly get what you order. A shame in 2020, a franchise like Red Robin is less able to do "special" order than McDonald's or Burger King.</Review>

< Text>
We had the Alaskan Cod fish and chips and I must say their's have risen to my favorite in the valley. Not too breaded, not oily but crisp, the tartar sauce was excellent and then the endless fries. I can only eat about one or two wedges and that's it; but very nice to offer. We sat at the bar during this visit since they have nice high chairs at the bar as well as bistro tables. I mention this for those of us who have trouble getting out of chairs lower to the floor. The bartender was excellent and checked back often to see how we were doing. I will put this place on my list when I want fish and chips or my partner a hamburger.
Easy access for those on wheelchairs. The bar has a lower section to eat at. Nice set up.< /Text>

< Text>
Red Robin is a great place for burgers and more!  The company seems to be consistent throughout the various locations.  Their free loyalty club is wonderful.  Many burgers choices, from size to toppings but havent EVER had a bad one.  Bottomless fries, they are known for but they have bottomless substitutions for those avoiding carbs.

House made salads, fish and chips, great shakes and desserts round out the menu with something for everyone.  If you can't decide, try Red's Tavern Double for a great juicy burger w/fries at 6.99.  And dont forget to check the loyalty club.  Every 10th burger on ur account is free!  Enjoy Red Robin!</Text>

<name>Patrick< /name><Time>1489977251284< /Time>< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< review>
Small parking lot for this restaurant‚Äã, in front of it though shares parking from the movie theaters. As soon as I walked in I was greeted and asked my party size and seating preference. Inside of the building was very clean and the staff was professionally dressed and friendly.

We sat at a bar booth and ordered drinks. Tables were clean and there is a kiosk at each table. Our waiter arrived and introduced herself and made us aware of happy hour and specials, very informative.

I ordered a beer, miller light in a tall glass for $4.50. They do not have a real good selection of alcohol, im surprised red robins have typically always been that way.

I ordered a burger and it was pretty busy. Shockingly wait time was very short! The burger was excellent too. Only thing I do not like is if you get fries with your meal, they give you a very small amount of fried in a small silver holder. Fries with a meal are bottomless meaning you can get as much as you want, just be prepared to ask your waiter multiple times to get more. If they just served a normal chunk of fries like they use to in the past that is typically enough to satisfy your french fry hunger.

Prices are great for what is provided, defenitely a good value. Once finished with my meal I could pay with the kiosk and even split the check with guests through the kiosk, as well as enter rewards phone number and what not. This is a great options because one of my pet peeves at any restaurant is when you pay with a card, you have to wait for the bill to be brought to you, wait for waiter to process it, come back and hand it back to write a tip. Usually when im done eating im ready to go and get impatient.

Great visit overall with some minor issues such as the lack of fries offered. Not enough to ruin the 5 star rating that they deserve here.<//review>
